[2026-01-12T04:52:10Z] Pavan Pamidimarri: Q.	X introduced a silver coin called rupiya, containing about 11.5 grams of pure silver, as the currency of his empire during his reign between 1540 and 1545. Panini and Chankaya had used the word several centuries earlier, but the modern rupee takes it definite form here. The East India Company made the rupee the standard currency of the lands it controlled in the subcontinent and beyond. Events that occurred thousands of miles away in the second half of the 19th century resulted in the price of silver crashing, eroding the value of the rupee relative to other gold-based currencies like the British pound sterling. The British exploited this to accelerate the loot of wealth from India. The system was remedied finally in 1899 with the rupee switching to an indirect gold standard. ID X and why the price of silver crashed. ‎<This message was edited>

[2026-01-12T07:11:44Z] మాन$: ⚡ QUIZ FORMAT: “PASS THE PRESSURE” ↵ (Power, psychology, and points on the line) ↵ 👥 Players ↵ 4–6 individual participants ↵ 1 Quiz Master (QM) ↵ 🎮 CORE MECHANIC (The Twist) ↵ QM asks a question (no buzzer initially). ↵ Any participant can buzz. ↵ The buzzer does NOT answer the question. ↵ Instead, the buzzer: ↵ Selects another participant to answer. ↵ Wagers their own points on that participant. ↵ 💰 WAGER RULES ↵ The buzzing participant (called the Primary) must wager: ↵ Minimum: 5 points ↵ Maximum: 50% of their current score ↵ The wager is locked before the answer is given. ↵ 🧠 OUTCOMES ↵ Outcome	Result ↵ Selected participant answers correctly:	Primary loses the wagered points ↵ Selected participant answers wrong:	Primary gains the wagered points ↵ Selected participant refuses / times out	. Treated as wrong ↵ 👉 The answering participant’s score does not change — only reputation is at stake. ↵ ⏱️ ANSWER RULES ↵ Selected participant has 10 seconds to answer. ↵ No pass, no hints. ↵ QM’s ruling is final. ↵ 🔄 OPTIONAL TWISTS (Use 1–2 max) ↵ 🎯 Double Dare ↵ Primary can declare “Double Dare”: ↵ Wager doubles. ↵ QM adds a follow-up question if the first is correct. ↵ 🛑 Shield Token ↵ Each participant gets one shield: ↵ Can refuse to answer once in the game. ↵ Question returns to QM; no points change. ↵ 👑 Kingmaker Clause ↵ If the Primary selects the current leader: ↵ Wager value is automatically doubled. ↵ 🏆 WIN CONDITION ↵ Fixed number of questions (e.g., 25). ↵ Or time-based (45 minutes). ↵ Highest score wins.
[2026-01-12T07:48:57Z] Sidhesh K K: X was the lowest denomination of currency in India. ↵ Mathematically, for other popular denominations ↵ Y=60X ↵ Z=40X ↵ A=7680X ↵ You would have heard X Y and Z in different phrases highlighting their negligible value. ↵ ID X Y Z A

[2026-01-12T08:48:21Z] Kartikey Pradhan: Correct. The family believed that when a person died, their sins could remain attached to the body or soul, preventing peaceful passage into the afterlife. [2026-01-13T04:22:21Z] Pavan Pamidimarri: 2.	The reason why uttarAyaNa (“northward journey” of the sun) is celebrated on the wrong day is a phenomenon called “X Y” or sometimes “Y of the equinoxes.” This phenomenon is caused mainly by gravitational tugs on the earth’s equatorial bulge from the moon and the sun, and one full cycle takes nearly 26,000 years. We can calculate that in the year 272 CE, makara sankrAnti coincided with the winter solstice, and since then the two occurrences have drifted apart. By the year 11,000 CE (i.e. 9,000 years in future), makara sankrAnti will occur in June.

[2026-01-13T15:41:06Z] Pavan Pamidimarri: from the video comments section, a detailed explanation for those math-minded: “Here's the best explanation I've found for resolving the paradox. ↵ Let's assume you're in a full stadium, and over the loudspeaker you ask all women who have exactly two children and at least one of them is a boy to raise their hands. ↵ Of the hands raised, you randomly select one woman.  In that case the odds of the other child being a girl are 66%, since you filtered out from a large set all the GGs. ↵ Now let's say, instead you announce you're looking for women with exactly two children where at least one boy was born on a Tuesday.  You'd get far fewer hands raised, of course, but the question is which hands were more likely to come down before you make your random selection?  The BGs and GBs are much more likely to drop than the BBs because the BBs have two chances to be true. ↵ If you keep adding constraints, like birth year, and first letter of name, etc, hands will keep dropping until one hand is left raised.   At that point, you're no longer selecting "randomly" from a pool of people meeting a filtered criteria, but a single person who's boy is so over-specified that the other sibling becomes a 50/50 independent event. ↵ In short the phrasing of the video's question is misleading because it's a single person giving info, but the math is assuming a draw from a random filtered pool.”

It comes from the understanding that those born into privilege have the duty to look beyond mere entitlement and pleasure, and must use their privilege and status for positive social change and for helping their fellow citizens. The concept of XY has found resonance in recent decades with the rapid rise of a cohort of meritocratic elite who many claim don’t possess the same level of social responsibility as elites of the past, as they believe they have ‘earned it’.
